  5. I've had toenail fungus problems for over 40 years. The products available, including this one that I use, Tea Tree Oil, all have one limiting factor in that they cannot penetrate the nail. The fungus lives under the nail and just laughs at you when you attempt to eradicate it. Nails are tough. You can attack the fungus at the tip of the nail, and perhaps on the sides, but at the bed of the nail, the fungus is about as safe and secure as the gold in Fort Knox.<br /><br />I'm not recommending this procedure for anyone, because it is a bit radical, and certainly could have side effects. I'm only telling you what has finally worked for me after trying a whole lot of other things for many years. I use a small handheld Dremel Rotary Grinding tool to create, between two and 4, small holes in the base of my infected toenails. Perhaps a 1/8th of an inch in diameter. I'm not into S&M and not thrilled with feeling pain, but it isn't as gruesome as it may sound. Normally there is little if any damaging of the skin at all. I've done it several times so I'm used to it, and I'm always very careful. I stop when I feel a slight burning sensation, and that is mostly actual heat produced by the grinding tip of the tool that I'm feeling. I stop on that spot momentarily, and go to another, and then come back to the first one a bit later. Of course my goal is to penetrate through the entire nail, or at least very close to, if not all the way through. I don't think it is necessary to go right to the skin, because it seems to work just as well both ways. Treatments will not go through the entire nail, but seem to penetrate a few thin layers just fine. Being very careful, I've only drawn blood once. It was like a small scratch. The big toe needs the most holes ground into it, a total of 4 in each, and there are 2 holes in each of the smaller toes. I then use Tea Tree Oil to kill the fungus by applying it at least twice a day when I wake up and before going to bed. If it is convenient, I will use it at other times such as after working out and then taking a shower.<br /><br />I mentioned that there could be side effects to this procedure. The major one is that unless I actually do the treatments to my toenails, meaning &#34;put some Tea Tree Oil or some other known fungus treatment on the nails&#34;, I could be opening them up for some other little bugs or bacteria that can also cause problems.<br /><br />I find that what is happening here, is that the fungus can't retreat to the base of my toenails for protection any more. As the toenail grows out, of course the holes move up the toe with the rest of the nail, chasing the fungus ahead of it. Chasing may be an improper term for something that goes this slowly. In this last treatment session, the holes have moved up about an 1/8 of an inch in two weeks. It will take 5 to 6 weeks or more for the entire nail to grow out. Products that claim clear clean toenails in one to two weeks are lying to you. The fungus is pretty tenacious, and will try to come back and probably will again at some point. I just do the same process again. The moment I see any trace of the fungus I bring out the Dremel tool again and start over.t at other times such as after working out and then taking a shower. I mentioned that there could be side effects to this procedure. The major one is that unless I actually do the treatments to my toenails, meaning &#34;put some Tea Tree Oil or some other known fungus treatment on the nails&#34;, I could be opening them up for some other little bugs or bacteria that can also cause problems. Our Tea Tree Oil is composed of less than 5% cineole and over 35% terpinen-4-ol which qualifies for \\"Pharmaceutical Grade\\", as established by the Australian Tea Tree Oil Association.\\" Now, maybe that means it *is* 100% TTO but just a weaker concentration or maybe it means that it's diluted; I'm not sure. Positives - - Cool, Clean Feeling - Diluted, potentially can work - Natural Negatives - - Cystic Acne - Strong Smelling - Minor Itching - Minor Redness Remember, the dilution process is extremely simple. If you're going to get 5% tea tree oil, simply do 95ml of carrier oil or water, and 5ml of tea tree oil to bring the total to 100%. You can see my before and after pictures from my study here: [...] Overall, I would use at your own risk. You will likely be more successful with tea tree oil if you do take the proper measures to dilute it down to the right percentage.

H20 = Distilled Water (leaves few or no water spots). TTO-H2O SOLUTION: 1/2 Tsp:16 oz. TTO-PFO MIXTURE: 25%:75% (1:3). DILUTE: Mix TTO with either H20 or PFO. Using TTO full strength may cause irritation. EVERYDAY USES: 1. Spray TTO-H2O solution on minor cuts, burns, sunburn, blisters, or cold sores. 2. Spray TTO-H2O solution on skin, hair, and clothes to use as an insect repellent or to repel spiders. 3. Spray TT0-H20 solution on mold. 4.
